Local News 151

Yesterday, Various Circles Commemorated the "March 18th" Massacre

A Memorial Meeting Was Held at the City Party Headquarters

At 9:00 AM yesterday, the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters convened various agencies and civic groups to hold a memorial meeting for the March 18th Massacre at the said City Party Headquarters. Over 300 representatives from various circles attended. Chen Dezheng presided, Wang Jinshan recorded, and Xu Yefu served as the master of ceremonies. After completing the rituals, Chen Dezheng delivered a report on the historical facts of the March 18th Massacre and the efforts that should be made for the March 18th commemoration. Afterwards, slogans were chanted and the meeting adjourned. The following is a record of Chen Dezheng's report:

"Fellow comrades, today is the March 18th Memorial Day. Everyone knows the origin of the March 18th Memorial Day. It commemorates a tragic event that occurred in Beiping on March 18th of the fifteenth year of the Republic of China (1926). During February and March of that year, Japanese imperialists, seeking to suppress the burgeoning revolutionary efforts in northern China, first unreasonably bombarded Dagu Port. They then joined with the eight nations involved in the Boxer Protocol and issued an ultimatum to the Duan Qirui government, demanding the removal of Dagu Port's coastal defenses and the cessation of all interference with the entry of foreign warships. This was tantamount to controlling China's northern coastal defense and was an extremely serious matter. If the Duan government had agreed to it, China's sovereignty would have suffered a great loss. Therefore, the people of the entire country were enraged, especially the citizens of Beiping, who feared that the Duan government would accept the humiliating ultimatum of the eight nations within 48 hours. Consequently, representatives from Beiping petitioned the Duan government on March 18th. However, Duan Qirui not only refused to accept their petition but also ordered his guards to open fire, wounding many representatives. When this news spread throughout Beiping, the citizens and students of various schools became even more furious. On the morning of March 18th, a mass meeting of Beiping citizens was held at Tiananmen Square. After the meeting, the crowd marched to Duan's private residence in Tieshizi Hutong, demanding that Duan immediately reject the eight nations' ultimatum. Duan, seeing the people's agitation, became enraged and, on the advice of figures like Zhang Shizhao, ordered the guards to open fire on the crowd from all sides, resulting in the deaths of fifty to sixty people, severe injuries to seventy to eighty, and countless minor injuries, creating an unprecedentedly bloody tragedy. This is a general overview of the historical facts of March 18th. Last year, at the West Lake Exposition, the revolutionary memorial hall displayed bloodstains from that day for us to see. From these tragic memories, we know the primary cause. Duan dared to instigate the guards to open fire and cause the tragedy because it was a manifestation of imperialist oppression of China. In other words, it was the imperialists using the hands of the Northern warlords to carry out a massacre of the revolutionary people of China. Secondly, if the Northern warlords had possessed even a shred of national spirit despite the imperialists' desire to massacre the Chinese people, they should have sternly rejected the eight nations' ultimatum long ago. The warlord government, in order to maintain its exploitative practices and its grip on power, catered to the imperialists in every way. The imperialists wanted them to do something, and they would do it. So, when the imperialists wanted them to act as executioners to massacre the Chinese people, they carried out the massacre. A third layer of meaning lies in the strange events that occurred alongside the imperialist oppression and the warlords' brutality. We know that the reason the March 18th crowd did what they did, for the crowd and students to charge with their bare hands, was due to the intentions of people like Xu Qian, who knew that under the pressure of imperialism, Duan Qirui would resort to slaughter. He had already led his family to the Legation Quarter in Dongjiaomin Lane. If he were a true revolutionary, he should not have done so. Therefore, we know that this was merely using the name of revolution to rally the masses, but in reality, it was betraying the revolution and the masses. The above points are the several important causes and facts of the March 18th event. From these, we derive the following lessons. The first lesson is that the March 18th incident occurred because imperialism sought to undermine the Chinese national revolution. Therefore, as long as imperialist oppression continues, China will not achieve freedom and equality. To achieve freedom and equality for China, we must follow Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings and strive to attack imperialism. After March 18th, imperialist oppression of China has continued unabated. In the north, there is Russian imperialism, in the east, Japanese imperialism, in the west, British imperialism, and in the south, French imperialism. Imperialists on all sides are aiming their cannons at China, ready to open fire. They have no goodwill to offer, so we must strive to attack all imperialists. The second lesson is that the March 18th incident occurred because of imperialism on one hand and the warlords' flattery of imperialism on the other. To thoroughly seek freedom and equality for China, we must fundamentally eliminate the Northern warlords. During the eighteenth and nineteenth years of the Republic of China, Northern warlords rose and fell one after another. Now, there are still remnants of warlords, large and small, such as Yan Xishan, uniting to disrupt the country. Therefore, as long as the Northern warlords exist, China cannot have hope for freedom and equality. Thus, in commemorating the March 18th Massacre, we should be even more pained by the continued existence of the remnants of the Northern warlords. To avenge the martyrs of the March 18th Massacre, we can only fundamentally eliminate the warlords under the leadership of the central government. The third lesson is that in addition to the crimes of imperialism and the Northern warlords, the facts of March 18th also include the fact that opportunists betrayed the revolution. We must be aware of this in the course of the revolution. Since the Northern Expeditionary Army captured Shanghai, there have also been many instances of opportunists betraying the revolution and betraying the masses, such as the Communist Party reorganisation faction, who have been engaging in acts of sabotage against the Chinese revolution under various deceptive pretexts. These kinds of figures have continued to exist from March 18th until now. If we are to commemorate March 18th and preserve the glorious history of the entire revolution, we must eliminate this force of false revolutionaries. Our commemoration today is very painful. For example, the revolutionary army reached Beiping, the site of the March 18th Massacre, a long time ago, but why has the revenge for the martyrs of March 18th not yet been exacted? This is because imperialism continues to oppress our country, the remnants of the Northern warlords continue to pursue their dream of seizing territory and accumulating private armies, and the forces of false revolutionaries and counter-revolutionaries who betray the revolution have not only not been eliminated, but are still using various despicable and cruel means to hinder the success of the Chinese national revolution. This is something that we should deeply recognise during this period. Therefore, I hope that our comrades understand the causes of the March 18th Massacre, remember the lessons learned from March 18th, abide by Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, and strive to complete the revolution under the leadership of the central government."

Precautions for March 18th 152

Yesterday was March 18th, the anniversary of the Beiping People's Revolutionary Memorial Day. The local Chinese-administered areas, due to the unsettled situation and the proliferation of rumours, announced a curfew yesterday for the sake of maintaining public order. The details of the precautions are listed as follows:

Nanshi: In the Nanshi area, in addition to the double patrols added to the police stations in various districts by the Public Security Bureau, armed police officers led by patrol officers were also stationed at key points to inspect vehicles and pedestrians. All members of the Nanshi Security Corps were also divided into teams to patrol the roads, and all members of the detective squad and female inspectors were also deployed in plain clothes. The curfew time would be advanced temporarily when necessary. Therefore, the Nanshi area was peaceful as usual yesterday.

French Concession: The French Concession police authorities issued an order the day before yesterday, instructing all detectives in all police stations to gather at their respective police stations and not to leave without authorization, so that they could be dispatched at any time. Armed Annamese police squads were also deployed to patrol the roads. All the iron gates at the junctions between the Chinese and French areas were completely closed around 7:00 PM, leaving only a few places where trams could pass through, and additional detectives were stationed to provide security.

Public Concession: The two areas of the Public Concession, Pudong and Puxi, where factories are clustered, were under particularly stringent precautions. Even more attention was paid between 7:00 PM and 9:00 PM in the evening. All vehicles and pedestrians had to undergo inspection, which was quite thorough.

Disturbances on Various Roads in the Public Concession Yesterday 153

Yesterday afternoon around 2:00 PM, sixty to seventy young men and women distributed leaflets and shouted slogans between Fujian Road and Fourth Road in the Public Concession. Upon hearing this, the Lao Zha Police Station immediately ordered Chinese and foreign detectives to rush to suppress them. Three people were arrested. After questioning by the chief, they were released as there was no major connection. Around 6:15 PM last night, more than a hundred young students gathered at an open space on Tokyo Road in Puxi to hold a meeting. The patrol officer at that location heard about it and immediately reported it to the police station. Chinese and foreign detectives arrested eight people and took them to the police station for investigation. Around 6:30 PM, a crowd gathered at the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Qujiang Road, distributing leaflets and shouting slogans. Two people were arrested by the police. It was also reported that similar movements occurred in the Hongkou area, and five people were arrested by the police.

Heavy Taxation on Chinese Silk by the French and Japanese 154

The National Goods Association Cables for Negotiations

The Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association recently sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the issue of export tax rates: "To Minister Ru Tang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Executive Yuan of the National Government in the Capital: We recently received your ministry's Yu Dai telegram, and upon reading it, we learned that in the Sino-Japanese treaty revision conference, the draft treaty proposed by our side did not have any reciprocal provisions regarding tariff matters. As for the full text of the new treaty, it is still under negotiation and cannot be copied and sent yet. We are responding specifically. Foreign Ministry Yu Yin, etc." After reading it, we were overjoyed and deeply moved by your adherence to the late Director's instructions on revolutionary diplomacy, negotiating and protecting the people's livelihood. However, at this critical moment, we cannot help but offer our sincere suggestions again, hoping to be adopted, which would be extremely fortunate. Our association has repeatedly received telegrams from various silk industry groups in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, Henan, Guangdong, and other provinces, stating that our country's tariffs are bound by agreements with the great powers and have always maintained a lenient attitude. Since the opening of trade, the doors have been wide open, and all comers are welcome. The tariffs collected are extremely low, resulting in foreign goods being sold extensively for over eighty years, filling the entire country, while our inherent national goods have been overthrown and gradually declined, leading to financial exhaustion and national weakness, creating a dangerous situation. This economic oppression, if not urgently remedied, will inevitably lead to national ruin. However, foreign goods coming to China are treated with sincerity and welcome by the whole country, while Chinese goods for export are often subject to heavy taxes and are clearly rejected. For example, Japan lists Chinese silk as a luxury item and collects a heavy tax of 100% of its value. In fact, it is even more than that. The Japanese customs arbitrarily raise the assessed value of Chinese silk, sometimes exceeding the cost by 1.3 times. Therefore, since the thirteenth year of the Republic of China (1924), our Chinese silk has not been able to be imported into Japan and Korea at all. The Chinese silk industry has suffered losses of more than tens of millions. The reason for the stagnation of domestic silk in recent years stems from this. Furthermore, last year, Vietnam newly implemented heavy taxes, increasing the original amount by dozens of times, which greatly affected Chinese silk. Since then, it has disappeared from exports, and this has been going on for years. Although our country's government and people have consistently protested, there has been no success. These facts clearly show that Japan and France are intentionally disregarding us and arbitrarily cutting us off. How can we tolerate this under the rule of the Qingbai Party? At this time when the Sino-Japanese and Sino-French treaties are beginning to be revised, we earnestly request that you, Minister, exert every effort to negotiate with Japan and France regarding this heavy taxation on Chinese silk, vowing to achieve the goal of abolition. Our people throughout the country are willing to be the backing force and fight together. Moreover, in today's China, which is economically oppressed and has backward production, the great powers are all around, eyeing us covetously, invading us overtly and covertly, sparing no effort. On the one hand, they use unequal treaties to expand production and sell it to our country, using our blood and sweat to increase their production. This cycle continues, and their desires are insatiable, while our blood and sweat are exhausted. If we do not strive to revive ourselves, national ruin will follow. On the other hand, they use the policy of protecting trade by increasing taxes, obstructing the development of our country's industries in many ways, implementing heavy taxes, and rejecting the shipment of Chinese goods. Alas, what injustice in the world is greater than this? Therefore, we specifically implore you to listen carefully and earnestly request that you, Minister, adhere to your principles and do not yield in the slightest, and not stop until the heavy taxes imposed by Japan and Vietnam on Chinese goods are abolished and equal treatment is achieved. The possibility of restoring our country's foreign trade depends entirely on this single lifeline. If successful, domestic goods will still have a day to be exported, and chronic diseases may be revived. The national economy and the people's livelihood will benefit from it. Otherwise, financial exhaustion and national weakness will lead to destruction. Therefore, this move is truly related to the survival of our entire Chinese nation, and we rely on you, Minister, to single-handedly hold up the sky and save us from this catastrophe. It is not only the millions of farmers, industrialists, and businessmen who will be grateful. We read in the newspaper yesterday that the draft Sino-Japanese tariff agreement has already been signed. What is the scope of the word 'agreement'? And has the heavy tax of 100% of the value of goods shipped from our country to Japan and Korea and collected by the Japanese customs been abolished in this treaty revision, or is the tax rate the same as the tax rate we collect on Japanese goods imported into our country? Our association, like a bird startled by the twang of a bow, is frightened by the sound of the string. We dare to send a special telegram to implore and await clear instructions. Wang Jianan, Wang Xingyi, and Wang Hanqiang, Standing Committee Members of the Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association, respectfully bow."

City Social Bureau Discusses Domestic Materials for Formal Attire 155

The City Social Bureau held a bureau affairs meeting yesterday to discuss practical measures for using domestically produced materials for formal attire. The general guidelines are as follows: the robe will be blue, the jacket will be black, the hat will be black for spring, autumn, and winter, white for summer, and the shoes will be black. The materials will be silk, hemp, and cotton for clothing, satin, velvet, and cloth for hats in other seasons, except for straw hats with plain black bands for summer, and satin, velvet, and cloth for shoes, as well as leather, but only leather that is confirmed to be domestically produced will be qualified. Samples of robes, jackets, shoes, and hats will be collected by the bureau from relevant factories and stores, and representatives from various circles will be invited to jointly select them. Once selected, a special name may be given to them (such as "formal attire satin" or "formal attire cloth"). The samples will also be distributed to various agencies and organizations to promote them. It is reported that the bureau has submitted the proposed measures to the city government for approval.

Suggestion to Move Henan Province Disaster Victims to the Border Regions 156

Hoping for Support from Philanthropists at Home and Abroad

The Shanghai office of the Zhenwu Association has received two telegrams from Zhu Zhenyuan, a member of the Henan war zone disaster relief, suggesting immigration and colonization of border areas, listing detailed measures for reclamation in the Northeast. Director Wang of the office believes that this method is very effective and intends to discuss it with Chairman Xu and present it for discussion at the Nanjing headquarters meeting. The telegrams are recorded as follows: The first telegram (omitted above) stated, "In recent years, disasters have struck various provinces, especially the Northwest. While providing relief with porridge kitchens and price stabilization is helpful in the short term, it is not a thorough solution. Moving immigrants to Liaoning and Ningxia provinces is the best policy. The soil there is fertile, with black soil seven to eight inches thick. For years, people from various provinces have voluntarily gone through the border, engaged in farming, and mostly settled down with their families, not wanting to return south because life there is easier and productivity is rich. Last year, Henan Province transported about 30,000 disaster victims. All workers boarded trains at various stations along the railway. Charitable organizations in Beiping provided supplies and special trains for direct transportation free of charge. After the disaster victims arrived in the Northeast, the Northeast authorities were very willing to find ways to settle and distribute them in various places, either to rush to reclaim land, to become tenant farmers, or short-term or long-term workers. Those with skills in cement, tile, or carpentry work received even better compensation, earning up to two yuan a day. Each year, official and private disaster relief consumes a large amount of funds. If this amount of money is distributed to the disaster areas, it would be easy to pay for immigration expenses, costing only two to three yuan to move one person. The benefits are great, and the comparison is obvious. It is hoped that charitable organizations and government officials at home and abroad will work together to plan for it." Zhu Zhong kowtows, Zhen. The second telegram stated, "The Zhen telegram should have arrived. Now, the Northeast Three Provinces' measures for treating disaster victims who arrive to reclaim land are explained in detail. Rushing to reclaim land means freely occupying land in areas designated by the government, planting and providing for oneself, and not paying land prices. After ten years of paying taxes, one can receive land. Claiming land means cultivating wasteland in areas designated by the government, temporarily not paying prices, and the government will provide assistance for food, housing, farming tools, livestock, seeds, and other expenses. After three years, land prices will be paid, with loans for land prices ranging from about five jiao to one yuan per mu. For tenant farmers, all expenses for food, housing, farming tools, seeds, and livestock before the harvest in the first year are provided by the landlord. The landlord only receives 20-40% of the profits, and never half. For external tenant farmers, housing is provided by the landlord, and the rest must be prepared by the tenant farmers. The tax is at most 20-30%. Short-term workers can earn at least seven to eight jiao to one yuan per day. The working time per year is about five months, which can earn more than one hundred and fifty yuan in wages. During the downtime, the employer still provides housing and rations. Long-term workers are divided into pure hired and semi-tenant farmers. Pure hired workers are paid annually, at least sixty to one hundred yuan, and up to one hundred and fifty yuan. Semi-tenant farmers do not discuss wages but designate thirty mu of land cultivated by the employer, with the income used as the worker's remuneration, collecting about six to seven dou per mu, with each dou weighing more than sixty jin. The income from thirty mu is worth about two hundred yuan. This method is mostly used to treat old workers. New workers can also ask for it. Please investigate and plan a large-scale relocation of disaster victims." Zhu Zhong kowtows, Yuan. It is hoped that charitable organizations from all walks of life will pay attention to the immigration matter mentioned by Mr. Zhu, enthusiastically support it, and make it a success, which is a blessing for the disaster victims.

After the report was completed, the following cases were resolved: (1) In accordance with the order to submit supplementary reports on the total amount of the budget and revenue and expenditure items for the seventeenth year and the statement of accounts for the seventeenth year, it was resolved that the General Affairs Section would be responsible for handling it. (2) On the case of rewarding the section chiefs who contributed to Beihui Road and the farmers who responded to the call, it was resolved that a letter would be sent to the 136th District to verify the contributors and report to the bureau, and the county government would be asked to commend them. (3) Pursuant to the order issued by the county government to draft the local budget for the eighteenth year, it was resolved that the clerical officer Ding of the General Affairs Section would handle it. (4) Pursuant to the order issued by the county government to distribute the General Economic Survey Form, Weights and Measures and Currency Survey Form, and Township Economic Survey Form of this county, the order was given to comply with the investigation and report it, and it was resolved that the clerical officer of the General Affairs Section would be responsible for the investigation. (5) Discussing the outline of the work report proposed by the Land Works Officer, it was resolved to amend and pass it.

Yesterday's County Finance Bureau 167

Meeting to Abolish the Dibao System

The Shanghai County Government previously received instructions from the Department of Civil Affairs to abolish the Dibao (local security) system. After deliberation by the county government, it was decided to implement it on April 1st, and the Finance Bureau was ordered to comply. The bureau chief, Li Zuyong, held a meeting at the bureau at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss the measures. Shen Zhou of the Land Production Office, Zheng Guozhai of the Education Bureau, Jiang Shouzhi of the Construction Bureau, and more than ten district chiefs from the county attended. Bureau Chief Li chaired the meeting, Tao Chungu recorded, and after the meeting, after performing the etiquette as usual, the chairman reported that the Department of Civil Affairs had stipulated that the township offices would be responsible for collecting the tax after the abolition of the Dibao system, but it should be discussed how to deal with it. After a long discussion, the following resolutions were made: (1) After the Dibao system is abolished, the township chiefs will be responsible for all matters related to distributing receipts and collecting taxes. (2) If there are abandoned tombs or households without heirs who have paid the taxes in advance, the township chiefs should verify the names of the households who paid the grain, the number of years, and the acreage of the land, and submit it to the district office, which will forward it to the Finance Bureau and submit it to the Department for allocation for local public use to avoid the burden of compensation. (3) In a picture where several townships are under jurisdiction, the township chief with the most jurisdiction is responsible for the collection. (4) The receipts for households that have not completed the winter tax payment in the eighteenth year will be handed over to the township chiefs for collection. The former Dibao will still be responsible for recovering the old debts of the sixteenth and seventeenth years. (5) Each district will set up a tax collection clerk, which will be supplemented by the Finance Bureau and directed by the district office to urge the township chiefs to be responsible for collection and distribution of receipts. (6) Each district should set up a money and grain sub-counter to facilitate the people to pay nearby. The Finance Bureau will prepare a budget and submit it to the Department for review. The meeting adjourned after deliberation and it was already 4:30.

Municipal Land Bureau 168

Reform of the Caojing Yangsi Tufang Boundaries Approved by Municipal Government Directive

The boundaries of maps and tufang in various districts of this city have always been extremely chaotic. After completing the surveying of the terrain of each district, the Municipal Land Bureau immediately began reorganizing them. It thoroughly reformed the boundaries of maps and tufang in the Special First and Second Districts of South Shanghai and submitted maps to the Municipal Government for approval and promulgation. Now, it is learned that the Caojing and Yangsi districts have both completed land surveying. The bureau has corrected the previously inconsistent boundary maps of the two districts, and re-compiled the maps and tufang to achieve uniformity. Furthermore, because the boundaries of the two districts are particularly intricate and have areas that are difficult to discern due to submersion, for the sake of reorganization, except for the borders that are adjacent to neighboring counties and areas not yet received, which cannot be easily altered due to the difficulty of reaching a final decision, within the jurisdiction of this city, a small part of the former Tangqiao District, south of Hengzhongjing Yangjiabang, is incorporated into the Yangsi District. The land south of Xinpu Huitang and Caohejing Port and west of Shang'ao Tang in the former Fahua and Pusong districts is incorporated into the Caojing District. As such, the boundary of Yangsi District is as follows: east to Nima Tang Xuejiabang, west to Huangpu River, south to Zhuangbang Qianliangbang Pengqibang Xujiabang, north to Huangzilou Yangjiabang, Hengchongjing, Jiangjiabang. The boundary of Caojing District is as follows: east to Huangpu River, west to Shang'ao Tang, Caohejing Port, Xinjinggang Jiebang, south to Caogang Chunshentang, Xiaocaibang, Changqiao Port, north to Longhua Port, Cai Dongjing, Xinpu Huitang. The boundaries of each district are demarcated by rivers, which greatly facilitates planning and research in business operations. The bureau has already submitted a request to the Municipal Government for a directive to approve the record.

Chamber of Commerce Requests Suspension of Alkali Tax 171

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram yesterday to the Jiangsu Financial Commissioner's Office, stating that: "According to letters from alkali merchants Hengli, Lida, Taikang, Yongda, Liumao, Yongtai, Shunda, and other alkali factories, it is reported that the Yanhui Miscellaneous Goods Guild's tax office is monopolizing the alkali commodity tax and forcibly collecting additional levies, causing extreme alarm among our colleagues. We immediately convened a meeting, and all agreed that Chinese alkali merchants lack raw materials. Although nominally 'native alkali,' in reality, half of the alkali powder is imported from foreign merchant Brunner Mond, which is already under economic pressure. Currently, these foreign merchant alkali factories, under the guise of 'native alkali,' are established in various provinces. In addition to import tariffs on raw materials, they do not suffer the pain of being levied taxes by monopolizing merchants. Now, Chinese alkali factories already have no hope of development and are barely able to maintain themselves. How can we impose further extortion? If alkali is resisted, it will inevitably become extinct. Now the government is determined to promote domestic goods. Whenever domestic goods compete with foreign goods, they are invariably given generous rewards. However, the guild is unaware of this purpose and is allowing outside monopolists to forcibly impose additional levies, causing colleagues to have no way to appeal and no means to save themselves. Therefore, we earnestly request your association to provide relief and also to order the cessation of tax collection to support domestic goods and alleviate merchant difficulties." Based on this investigation, foreign alkali is rampant, and native alkali already has little hope of survival. The situation is real. If arbitrary and harsh levies are imposed again, the only remaining native alkali factories will inevitably face higher costs and reduced sales, not only failing to compete with foreign alkali but also potentially leading to shutdowns. This is expected. At this time, when the abolishment of likin is being implemented, this kind of evil practice of monopolizing merchants collecting taxes is even more unnecessary. Based on the above, we hereby urgently request your office to investigate and approve an order to stop it, in order to maintain the remaining line of native alkali. We are deeply grateful. The Shanghai Special Municipality Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee respectfully reports."

Japanese Ships Expand Shipping to China 177

Dalian Yingkou Route Increases Ships. The Dalian Steamship Company has seen thriving shipping business last year on Shanghai, Dalian, and Tianjin routes. Profit alone on the Shanghai route was more than one million yuan. Therefore, while new ships are being built in Japan, there are plans to expand shipping routes in China's waters, adding new South China routes, which have already been decided. Now that Yingkou is thawed and Niuzhuang has a large amount of goods, the company has decided to open a new route between Shanghai and Yingkou while Chinese ships have not fully resumed operations. Five 2,000-ton ships are planned to be deployed. The company's president, Yasuda Matsu, has come to Shanghai from Dalian with General Affairs Section Chief Shimada to discuss the expansion plan with the Shanghai president.

Osaka Fuzhou Line Raises Prices. The Japanese ships on the Shanghai-Fuzhou route have been doing good business in recent months. Both cargo and passengers are crowding the Osaka Company in this port, which has three ships sailing to Fuzhou. Due to the increase in passengers recently, it was decided yesterday, citing the preciousness of gold and cheapness of silver, that from April 1st, the price of first-class cabins from Shanghai to Fuzhou will be raised from 30 yuan to 36 yuan, and the price of third-class cabins will be raised from 12 yuan to 14 yuan. Tickets from Shanghai to Taiwan will be charged in Japanese yen, approximately 40% higher than the original price.

Negotiations on the Fairness Collision Case. The Fair Ship of the China Merchants Bureau was damaged by the Dazhou Maru of the Kobe Daifuku Company, causing losses of 50,000 to 60,000 yuan. After the China Merchants Bureau filed a complaint, the Japanese ship telegraphed back, ordering the China Merchants Bureau to send representatives to Kobe or Nagasaki to negotiate. The China Merchants Bureau has telegraphed back, refuting this, stating that since the accident occurred in the Yangtze River in China, negotiations should be held in Shanghai. The Daifuku Company is requested to send a fully authorized representative to Shanghai as soon as possible, or to negotiate with Mitsui & Co. on its behalf. The matter will proceed after the Japanese side responds.

News Roundup on Rescuing Stranded Ships 179

Xinming Has Been Towed to Tianjin. The China Merchants Bureau's Xinming ship was stranded in the Baihe River due to shallow water and heavy load. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Later, the Shanghai Bureau telegraphed Tianjin, ordering a lighter to unload some of the cargo from the Xinming ship first to reduce the weight, and then a small tugboat to rescue it. Yesterday afternoon, the Shanghai Bureau received another telegram from Tianjin stating that the Xinming ship had been towed to Zizhu Forest in Tianjin at 11 am on the 18th. The ship was undamaged, and the passengers landed safely.

Baling Will Sail to Shanghai. The Nisshin Company's Baling Maru, which ran aground off Nan'ao Island, requested the Tokyo Salvage Company to send the salvage ship Haiyuan Maru to Nan'ao to assist in the rescue, first patching the holes and then pumping out the seawater. Yesterday, the chief shipowner, Takeshita, telegraphed again, reporting that the towing was successful and that the ship would not go to Hong Kong but would go to Shantou immediately to load coal and sail to Shanghai on Thursday. However, all the cargo on the ship was lost on the 19th.

The Sanbei Company's Longshan ship, which was damaged at the Yitaixing Wharf in the Huangpu River, has had its stern rudder, impeller, and other parts repaired after ten days of rush work. Due to the shortage of rice in Shanghai, Siam has over one million shi of foreign rice to be shipped to Shanghai. British and Japanese shipping companies are competing to send ships to load it. The Longshan ship is also scheduled to go to Yangon today to transport rice to Shanghai. Two Railways Issue Round-Trip Sightseeing Tickets 183

Available from March 20th with a Seven-Day Validity Period

Liu Chengchang, General Manager of the Traffic Department of the Two Railways Administration, believes that the scenic spots along the two railways are numerous. Now, with the beautiful spring scenery, it is a great time for the public to admire the mausoleum of the Premier, adjust their spirits, and enjoy the mountains and rivers. Therefore, he specially submitted a request to the director and, starting from the 20th of this month, issued first, second, and third-class round-trip sightseeing tickets between Beijing and Shanghai, between Shanghai North Station and Hangzhou, between Shanghai South Station and Hangzhou, and between Fanwangdu and Hangzhou. A round-trip ticket on a special express train is 19.2 yuan for first class and 9.6 yuan for second class, plus a 5% surcharge for traffic improvement.

Dispute Over Using Concession Water and Electricity in Yuqing Lane, Zhabei 184

Yuqing Lane on North Sichuan Road is entirely located in the Chinese territory. Previously, because the Chinese water pipes and electric wires had not yet reached, the lane used the water and electricity of the concession. The lane originally had five back doors leading to Changchun Road, so Chinese police officers were also stationed there for patrol. In the spring of the 16th year, when the National Revolutionary Army arrived in Shanghai and was in the initial stage of takeover, for some unknown reason, the owner of the lane, Li Jigu (said to be the youngest son of Li Hongzhang), suddenly completely blocked the original back doors and hired concession gatekeepers and patrolmen. Unexpectedly, this caused the concession authorities to levy patrolman fees. The lane then reopened the blocked back doors to resist the payment of patrolman fees. There has always been a precedent between the Chinese and concession areas that houses on the boundary that can通达reach the Chinese territory are under the jurisdiction of the Chinese territory, and the concession has no right to interfere. However, the Public Works Bureau stated that if the fees were not paid, the water supply would be cut off and the electricity flow would be terminated, causing great panic among the residents. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, recognizing that the recovery of the lane's water and electricity could not be delayed, immediately supervised the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to connect the lane's water pipes and negotiated with the Concession Electric Company to recover the lane's electricity supply. At the same time, it negotiated with the owner to voluntarily switch to Chinese water and electricity. Unexpectedly, the concession authorities showed some agreement, but the Li owner ignored it. In September of the 17th year, the Public Utilities Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and Finance Bureau jointly sent a letter to the owner, advising him to take into account national sovereignty and switch to Zhabei water and electricity. However, his family, using the excuse of leaving Shanghai, returned the original letter. Subsequently, the Public Security Bureau ordered the police to personally deliver the letter to his Western rent collector, Aierde, who also refused to accept it. The case has been suspended for years without resolution. In January of the 19th year, because the lane was building new houses, the Public Utilities Bureau again instructed the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to negotiate with the Shanghai Electric Power Company to recover the lane's electricity supply. As a result, the Electric Power Company first transferred the households in the lane to the Zhabei Company, which was somewhat resolved. As for the water supply, the Zhabei water pipes had previously been connected to Changchun Road and recently extended from Changchun Road to Sichuan Road. Therefore, the new houses there could have used Zhabei tap water. However, the Li owner again blocked the back doors of the new houses and entrusted the Concession Water Company to install water pipes, resulting in the conflict between Chinese police and Japanese police reported yesterday. At the time, Chief Qu of the Fifth District, First Precinct, argued reasonably and opened the back doors, so there should be no problem with police authority. However, it is not known whether the Li owner can repent and voluntarily switch to Chinese tap water to preserve a share of sovereignty for the country. The joint letter from the Public Utilities Bureau, Finance Bureau, and Public Security Bureau to the Li owner on September 19 of the 17th year is excerpted below: We hereby inform you that the North Sichuan Road Yuqing Lane, owned by your organization, is located in the Chinese territory, but the use of water and electricity from the Public Concession has caused the Public Works Bureau to levy patrolman fees, which residents resist paying. This is extremely detrimental to national sovereignty. I believe that you are a national citizen who loves and protects national rights and should share the same enthusiasm. You should remove the concession water and electricity in the lane immediately and have it supplied by the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company in order to save the situation and prevent aggression. The company has long been prepared to supply water and electricity to the lane, and the prices are the same as those in the concession. You only need to notify them to install it to make it happen. Furthermore, Yipin Lane on Baoshan Road is owned by the foreign merchant Yipin Bank. It also used concession tap water, but the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company recently recovered the supply with the order of this Public Utilities Bureau, and the bank did not object since the lane belongs to the Chinese territory. Since the lane is Chinese property, there is even less reason to use concession water and electricity and harm national rights. We have specially prepared this letter to inform you. Please reply so that we can instruct the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to lay pipes and supply electricity to the residents. Sincerely, Mr. Li Jigao.

Water and Electricity Industry 185

[PRequest to Amend Electricity Regulations Adopted and Explained Separately by the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau

The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau has supervised and controlled the installation of electrical equipment in the city, and has issued five types of regulations successively: Regulations for the Management of Electrical Material Stores and Electrical Contractors, Detailed Rules for the Punishment of Violations by Electrical Material Stores and Electrical Contractors, Regulations for the Management of Electricians and Apprentices Installing Wires for Electrical Users, Regulations for Indoor Wiring for Electrical Users, and Regulations for the Inspection of Electrical Equipment in Public Places. Each has strict provisions. In the middle of last month, the Water and Electricity Industry Branch of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee, believing that the regulations and the Guidian Business Regulations of the Chinese Electric Company were detrimental to the future development of electrical appliances, submitted 36 items that should be amended, along with the reasons, to the Public Utilities Bureau through the Chamber of Commerce for review. The content of the submission included requests for reduced fees, requests for extended deadlines, requests for the complete deletion of certain articles in certain regulations, and requests for the strict enforcement of already stipulated articles. The situation was quite complicated. After careful review, the bureau believed that, except for three items—the deadline for electrical material stores and contractors to retrieve their security deposits, the notification procedure after electrical equipment inspection fails, and the grace period for electricians or apprentices to renew their licenses annually—which could be adopted, the rest lacked sufficient reason. It was learned yesterday that the reasons in the original submission have been explained item by item and sent to the Chamber of Commerce for reference and notification.

Prohibition of Building Straw Houses on Roadside Land 186

The Police Department of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways issued a notice yesterday to the police chiefs of each section, stating that: "According to the Administration Bureau's Instruction No. 265, the General Affairs Department reported that, after checking, it was found that villagers often build straw houses on the surplus land of various stations along the two railways. This not only infringes on property rights but also hinders aspects of appearance, sanitation, fire prevention, and public security. This bureau has repeatedly proposed to clear them, but the villagers, due to livelihood concerns, are content with their makeshift arrangements and refuse to demolish and relocate within the specified time, causing the reorganization plan to be frustrated. Recently, for example, the straw houses near the Nanjing freight yard suddenly caught fire. According to the bureau's reports, the police section was ordered to prohibit rebuilding. However, rent collector Liang Tianyou reported that when he went to Jiaxing to collect rent, he heard that a straw house had been lost to carelessness on the surplus land and rushed to investigate. Three straw houses had already been rebuilt. It seems that after being built and burned, they are built again. The stations face the risk of fire, and the straw houses cannot be cleared. It is proposed to order the police of each section to strictly prohibit the construction of new straw houses on the roadside land in the future. If straw houses are burned, the rebuilding must be strictly prohibited. Is this appropriate? Please, Director, review and implement accordingly." Based on this, it is hereby ordered to the police chiefs of each branch of the two railways police to pay attention. In the future, the construction of new straw houses on the roadside land, whether rebuilt or newly built, must be strictly prohibited to avoid danger and facilitate the promotion of railway administration. This is extremely important.

Social Affairs Bureau Prohibits Tricky Eyeglasses 187

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau investigated the Shanghai newspaper report of a "scientific eyeglasses scam" by the Taili Foreign Firm. Also, the American "Light of Salvation" advertisement published in various newspapers on March 13 and March 14 was investigated by personnel. It was reported that the eyeglasses were sold by the Maochang Eyeglasses Store and had conspicuous advertising flags. According to the store clerk, the eyeglasses were made by scientists at the American Taili Foreign Firm and boasted various advantages, many of which were unbelievable. It was observed that wearing these eyeglasses would likely be harmful rather than helpful, and the materials were of poor quality but the price was high, as reported in the Shanghai newspaper. Such insinuations of foreign merchants, using the name of science to deceive the world and swindle money, are truly inappropriate. It is requested to prohibit them. Many Good Plays at the Xunyuan Restaurant 188

One Wave Subsides, Another Rises

Wang Yingwu Does Not Sue Wu Zhaoyi, Wu Zhaoyi Sues Chang Yunheng. The Shanghai stage production of the Peking opera "Xunyang Tower," with Gao Qingkui playing Song Jiang and Wang Yingwu playing the general, premiered on the fifteenth night. Wang, the actor, was slightly late in putting on his hat, causing a slight disruption. After the performance, Gao and Wang had a quarrel backstage. Wu Zhaoyi, Gao's bodyguard, intervened and brandished a handgun, appearing ready to act. Chang Yunheng, the backstage manager, dissuaded them. Wang, unwilling to accept this, reported it to the police, who dispatched detectives to arrest Wu and seize opium paste and other items from Gao's residence. They were handed over to the Provisional Court, which ordered Wu to be detained and the opium paste and other items to be confiscated. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Wu was detained until 7 pm the day before yesterday, when his lawyer, Fan Gang, applied to the court for bail. The original trial judge, Gao Junxiang, approved the bail of 100 yuan, and Wu was released. Thus, he did not experience the flavor of a prison cell overnight. Yesterday afternoon at 2 pm, Judge Gao reopened the hearing. Wu surrendered himself as scheduled. However, the plaintiff, Wang Yingwu, had been persuaded by friends and did not want to pursue the case. He requested the withdrawal of the charges in court. Judge Gao approved the request. Thus, the matter was over. However, Wu Zhaoyi suddenly filed a lawsuit in court, suing Chang Yunheng. The judge considered this a separate case and would review it later. Truly, as the saying goes, "One wave has just subsided, and another rises."

Xing Zhigang's Letter Requesting the Removal of Obstacles in the Navigation Channel 189

Yesterday, Xing Zhigang and others, representing ship owners in Pudong and Puxi, submitted a document to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, requesting the removal of obstacles in the navigation channel. The document stated that the navigation channel has been repeatedly obstructed and pleaded for the respective elimination of these obstructions to benefit shipping and travel. It noted that the Pudong and Puxi areas are vast, and all the ships from various cities and towns, after arriving in Shanghai with the tides, used to dock at the Nan Huiguan Wharf and the Wanyu Gongyi Wharf without any issues. However, the Wanyu Wharf has become dilapidated and collapsed over the years, making it impossible to dock there. Consequently, many ships gather around the Nan Huiguan area. Furthermore, large kiln cargo ships that used to dock at Xuejiabang and Santai Wharves have also occupied these wharves to load and unload goods, causing ships from Pudong and Puxi to anchor far out in the river, with no wharves to rely on. The most egregious issue is that lumber merchants along the Huangpu River scatter various timbers on the river surface, extending beyond the dredging line by several tens of feet. When ships arrive, passengers have to walk on uneven timber rafts to get ashore, which is very dangerous when the tide surges. Such a perilous situation can only be truly appreciated by those who have experienced it firsthand. Moreover, when passengers disembark from the ships, they face another obstacle: groups of old women from the dock rowing teams gather and stand on the gangplanks of each ship as the tide recedes, extorting one copper coin from each passenger. Those who refuse to pay are blocked from passing, preventing the public from proceeding, and some are even pushed into the river. These abhorrent practices are particularly detestable. All of the above situations constitute obstacles to navigation. As municipal reforms are underway, attention should also be paid to the security and order on the waterways. Therefore, this petition is respectfully submitted to your office, earnestly requesting that you promptly instruct the cargo ships to return to their original wharves, restrict the lumber merchants from piling up timber, and eliminate the old women of the boat crews who extort money, so that travelers from the surrounding villages can embark and disembark safely, without any danger. This is what the petitioners earnestly pray for day and night.

A Quack Doctor Old Woman Was Swindled 194

Thief Caught on the Way, Sentenced to Two Months in Prison

Liu Jinlin, a 24-year-old man from Hunan, went to the house of Shao Wang, an old woman who worked as a quack doctor, at 1 Wu Xing Lane, Beile Road, in the French Concession several days ago. He swindled her out of forty pieces of clothing, including a gray squirrel fur cheongsam, worth over two hundred yuan, which he pawned for money and fled. The victim reported the incident to the police station, requesting an arrest. The victim found him and brought him to the police station. After questioning by the police chief, he was ordered to be detained while the stolen goods were retrieved. Yesterday, he was sent to the French Court. Judge Zhu heard the case in the criminal court. The plaintiff, Shao Wang, stated that on the morning of the 13th of this month at 10:00 AM, the defendant came to her house and said that he was a servant of the Wang Mansion on Julida Road. Because the young lady of the house was ill, they had sought treatment from many famous doctors without success and had even consulted a hospital that demanded 1,200 yuan in medical fees. The young lady was willing to pay 800 yuan, but the hospital still refused, so she did not receive treatment. Now, he had come to ask her to provide medical treatment, and if she could cure the young lady, she would receive a large reward, which would also be beneficial for her. After speaking, he left. Then, at 2:00 PM that afternoon, he came again, looking very anxious, and said that the young lady was watching a movie at the Paris Cinema and that she should wear fancy clothes and quickly go to the mansion to wait. If she did not wear good clothes, she might be stopped by the gatekeeper from entering. Seeing his urgent manner, the woman believed him. She borrowed four pieces of clothing, including a gray squirrel fur cheongsam, from her neighbor and returned home.

She put them on, but the defendant suddenly claimed that she was a quack doctor and did not need to wear such good clothes. She should wear her old, tattered clothes, but leave the fur clothes at home temporarily. If the young lady saw that her clothes were old and looked down on her, she could come back home and change. The woman deeply believed him and wore her old clothes, following him to the Wang Mansion to treat the illness. Unexpectedly, when they arrived in front of the Paris Cinema, the defendant falsely claimed that the young lady was inside watching a movie and asked her to wait at the entrance for a moment until the young lady came out and they would go to the mansion together to treat the illness. After a while, the defendant suddenly disappeared. At that time, the woman became suspicious, knowing that something was wrong. She immediately returned home and was shocked to find that the defendant had taken the opportunity to go to her house and swindle her daughter out of all the clothes. Upon learning this, the woman was extremely frightened and immediately reported it to the police station. She then sent people to search everywhere and finally found him on the street several days ago, reported the incident to the police, and arrested him. However, the woman had been greatly frightened and had not been able to eat or sleep for three days and nights. The defendant's actions were in violation of the law, and she requested a severe investigation. When questioned, the defendant Liu Jinlin admitted to swindling the clothes without denial. Judge Zhu sentenced Liu to two months in the Western Jail as a warning and ordered the stolen clothes to be returned to the plaintiff.

Case of Abusing a Maid 195

After Appeal, the Original Sentence of Two Years Imprisonment Was Overturned

Feng Ye, a widow from Guangdong residing in Hongan Lane, Haining Road, was previously arrested by the police and sent to the Provisional Court for beating her maid, Liu Ying, after Wan Xu, a woman living in the same building, reported the incident. She was sentenced to two years in prison, as reported earlier. However, Feng Ye was not satisfied with the sentence and hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to file an appeal. The appellate court held a hearing on the case the other day. According to the accuser, Wan Xu, she knew that Feng Ye often beat the maid, and on the eighth day of the first month, she severely beat Liu Ying again and poured cold water on her head. She felt that this was unjust, so she reported it to the police. Lawyer Zhan then asked if she had seen the beating. The woman replied that Feng Ye had closed the door when she was beating the maid, so she only heard crying. He then asked how she knew that cold water had been poured on her head if the door was closed. The woman replied that after she reported the incident to the police, she and the police went into the appellant's room and saw a basin of water and water on the floor, so she assumed that water had been poured on her. According to the witness Yi Ye, the appellant was her fourth aunt, and the girl was fostered in the appellant's house and was treated very well, with no abuse at all. Judge Chou ordered Liu Ying to be brought in for questioning. At first, the girl only cried and refused to speak. The police lawyer claimed that this was because the appellant was in court, so the girl was afraid to speak frankly. Judge Chou immediately ordered the bailiff to take the appellant out of the courtroom and told Liu Ying not to be afraid and to speak truthfully. The girl then said that although she was often beaten, it was not very painful and that she did not want her foster mother to be convicted and imprisoned because of this. The debate then began. Lawyer Zhan argued that the appellant's beating of Liu Ying was an undisputed fact, but that beating a daughter was a form of parental supervision over the conduct of their subordinates and was a remedy for parents and teachers to correct the misconduct of their children. The issue that should be studied was whether the appellant's exercise of this supervisory power was appropriate and whether it exceeded the necessary extent.

He argued that the appellant had only given a slight reprimand at the time, which was certainly not as severe as the witness Wan Xu had said. Moreover, Wan Xu's testimony was full of contradictions and was not credible. As for Yi Ye's behavior, it could be seen that the appellant did not have excessive behavior towards Liu Ying. Furthermore, this case was sentenced according to Article 293 of the criminal law, and Article 302 of the same law required a formal complaint. Although Liu Ying was young, she was knowledgeable and had already expressed that she did not want to punish the appellant, so this case could not be established. He requested that the original sentence be overturned and the appellant be declared innocent. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Chou and Assessors Shen and Li announced the verdict in court, overturning the original sentence and releasing the appellant.

The officer ordered Wu to pay two dollars as a warning.

Pig Boat Escaped From Pirate Bullet Rain 202

Two Pirate Ships Pursued Closely and Escaped Near Songkou

According to the crew of the Jiangbei pig boat Xu Hengmao yesterday, the pig boat loaded more than 180 live pigs from Zhanghuang Port and came to Shanghai. The night before, when it arrived on the sea off Qilipu, it suddenly saw two pirate ships approaching from afar. Because they knew their intentions, they immediately set sail and tried to escape. Fortunately, the pig boat had strong driving force and broke through. Unexpectedly, the pirate ships opened fire and ordered them to stop. Because the pig boat ignored them, the bandits became angry and opened fire. It felt like bullets were raining down, and all the crew members were panicked. Fortunately, they were far away and it was difficult for the bullets to hit. The two pirate ships pursued for dozens of miles, but when they reached the Lion Grove sea area downstream of Liuhe, the bandits did not dare to pursue any further because they were close to Songkou. The pig boat finally escaped. Upon inspection of the boat, there was no damage, but all the crew members were frightened. The pig boat had been inspected yesterday and was allowed to open in Shanghai.

Merger of American Chase Bank and Chemical Bank 203

Still using the name Chemical Bank

The Shanghai Chase Bank recently received a telegram from its New York headquarters that the parent company of the bank, Chase Communications Trust Company, is currently discussing a merger with the New York Chemical National Bank. The plan was submitted to the board of directors of both parties yesterday. According to the current plan, after the merger, it will still use the name Chemical Bank, and Albert Lee, president of Chase, will serve as the new president. In the future, the new bank's capital reserve will reach 250 million U.S. dollars, and the retained earnings and undistributed dividends will exceed 27 million yuan. In addition, before the merger, it will first absorb the various state trust companies in New York. The purpose of the merger is purely to facilitate depositors and customers, and all current contracts and business policies will remain unchanged.

Second District Precinct Captures Notorious Bandit 210

Around 2 PM the day before yesterday, the Second District General Precinct of the Nanshi Public Security Bureau received a tip-off from an informant, stating that notorious bandit Wang Yunxiang had been committing numerous crimes within the French Concession. It was reported that he was to pass by Wansheng Bridge near the Old West Gate with his mistress. The informant requested that officers be dispatched to apprehend him swiftly. After reporting to Warden Wang, Detective Cao Junda was secretly instructed to lead the entire team, armed with weapons, to await the suspect. Shortly thereafter, the bandit was spotted riding in a rickshaw with his mistress, heading south from Wansheng Bridge. The informant identified him clearly. Detective Ma Azeng bravely stepped forward and grabbed Wang. Unexpectedly, the bandit pulled out a handgun and fired at Ma, hitting him in the left thigh. As he attempted to fire a second shot, Ma's colleagues quickly seized the bandit's hand holding the gun. One finger accidentally inserted into the trigger guard, holding on tightly, preventing the second shot. The detectives then rushed forward together, apprehended him, seized the gun, and brought him and his mistress back to the precinct. After stern interrogation by Warden Wang, the bandit confessed to being 38 years old, from Yancheng, and currently residing at No. 16, Fuxing Lane, Pingji Road in the concession. He also revealed the location of hidden weapons and accomplices. His mistress, when questioned, identified herself as Li Baobao, 20 years old, from Yangzhou, and formerly a prostitute at the Qinglian Pavilion on Fourth Avenue. She claimed that Wang had redeemed her and that it had not been a month yet, and that she was unaware that Wang was a bandit, pleading for leniency. Based on the confession, Warden Wang dispatched the original team of detectives to a desolate tomb area in Tanziawan Township, Zhabei, where they discovered 144 bullets hidden under a coffin. Furthermore, at around 6 AM yesterday, they secretly went to Zhabei, coordinating with the First Sub-precinct of the Fourth District, and apprehended a Jiangbei native named Wenlin, along with two other suspects, at No. 2, Haixiang Lane, Gonghe Road. All were brought back to the precinct for questioning. The bandit Lü also confessed to colluding with Wang in numerous robberies. After clarifying the facts, Warden Wang plans to submit a document to the Judicial Section today for further investigation. The injured detective, Ma Azeng, is not in serious condition and is expected to recover soon.

Pedestrian Run Over by Public Bus 213

Qian A'er, a 61-year-old man from Pudong, came to Shanghai yesterday morning for business. At 7 PM, while walking along the Bund at Nanjing Road, he was suddenly knocked down by a No. 9 public bus. Both legs were broken, and he bled profusely. The police on duty arrived, recorded the driver's license number, and transported the injured man to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Reward Offered for Apprehension of Robbers in the Four Banks Case 214

The Public Concession General Police Department announced that on the 13th of this month, at 2 PM, the preparatory treasury of the Zhongnan and other four banks dispatched a treasurer accompanied by armed police to the Tongshang and HSBC banks to deposit $46,000. Near the back door of the Tongshang Bank, they were ambushed by several robbers, who seized the police, took their guns and whistles, and stole the bags of money. They boarded a car that was waiting on the roadside, forced the driver out, and sped away. Later, the car was found in the Chinese territory near the Old North Gate. Fearing that the robbers were hiding in the Chinese territory, a letter was sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau ordering a joint search. It was stated that if the stolen money was recovered, a reward of 10% would be offered. Director Yuan has instructed all district precincts and teams to cooperate in the search.

Inquiry into Compensation for Japanese Ship Collision Case 215

Jin Hongyuan, 46 years old, from Teng County, Shandong, has been a boatman for many years. Yesterday, he reported to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau Water Patrol Team that on the 2nd of this month, his boat was loaded with 4,000 cans of kerosene and was being transported to Huzhou. Unfortunately, at around 3 PM that afternoon, the boat was traveling south on the Huangpu River, on the Puxi side, when it was rammed amidships by the Dade steamship of the Japanese Jiayun Shipping Company, causing it to break apart. A large amount of the cargo was lost, and his 89-year-old grandmother, wife, and other family members relied on the boat as their home. With the boat destroyed and all their possessions lost, they are now bankrupt and struggling to survive. He requested that a letter be sent to the Japanese shipping company to seek compensation for the losses. After receiving the report, the team leader stated that since it involved a ship collision, he would order detectives to investigate and verify the facts before processing the matter.

Scheduled Election for the Chinese Taxpayers' Association 216

The election of new directors for the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession has been scheduled for the 22nd of this month. The ballots will be counted at the Bankers' Association. It is said that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office has been asked to send observers.

Suzhou National Goods Touring Group After Arriving in Shanghai 217

The Audience Expresses Satisfaction

The Suzhou silk and satin factories jointly organized a national goods touring group. All the members of the group transported hundreds of kinds of novel silks and satins to Shanghai, which are displayed in the Penglai Market in Xiaoximen in this city for people to buy at low prices, in order to promote national goods and help with the disaster relief in Zhejiang. Groups from this city who went to welcome them included Wang Jie'an and Wang Hanqiang, chairman of the China National Goods Maintenance Association, Chen Yiting, chairman of the Citizens' Association for the Promotion of National Goods, and Xu Genghua of the Joint Association of Mechanized National Goods Factories. They went to Penglai Market to arrange the meeting place, and the members of each group displayed their goods. The exhibition began the day before yesterday. People from all walks of life in this city went to visit and purchase them enthusiastically, all saying that the prices were low and the quality was high, expressing satisfaction. It is also a good sign for the future of national goods.

Yesterday, the U.S. Commercial Officer announced the following statistics on U.S. trade with China for the 18th year: Under exports, cotton was 23,149, petroleum was 27,606, automobiles were 23,296, machinery and electrical equipment were 10,314, iron and steel were 8,681, lumber was 5,423, and wheat flour was 15,341. Under imports, raw silk was 61,597, leather was 7,194, wool was 12,503, fur was 9,230, tung oil was 14,972, tea was 1,751, and cotton was 2,635. All of the above are in units of thousands of U.S. dollars. Compared with the 17th year, China's main exports have decreased considerably.

Ding Runxiang has been recovering at the Chinese and Western Sanatorium since being brutally beaten by a Russian officer. It is said that his left eye, which was most severely injured, has been successfully treated by the renowned ophthalmologist Wu Kexi and his eyesight has been restored. However, its appearance may be disfigured. Although the internal injuries have been treated by the French forensic doctor Lang Beian and the famous trauma specialist Qin Genrong, they have not been alleviated. On the evening of the 9th, he vomited severely again and is now resting to recover as soon as possible. Various organizations, such as the Pudong Association and the Pudong Public Office, have sent representatives to question the French Consul, and others such as the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce have also sent people to investigate the facts and express their condolences, which were received by Mrs. Ding. As for the public and private lawsuits in this case, Ding's family said that they had engaged the lawyer Di Baike to handle the matter.

Residents of Jingyi Lane Oppose Renovation of Houses 226

The houses in Jingyi Lane, Malang Road, French Concession, have been built for five years. Recently, the landlord posted a renovation notice in the lane, ordering the tenants to move out quickly. All the tenants were panicked and held a general meeting of all the tenants at the Nanyang Bridge Business Federation at 9 PM yesterday. Thirty-two tenants arrived and elected Chen Yulin as chairman. He reported the age of the houses in this lane and the landlord's notice. After discussion, the resolutions were as follows: (1) Establish a tenant union; (2) Unanimously oppose the landlord's illegal demolition of houses; (3) Not to be succumbed to money, all swear not to move; (4) If necessary, raise funds to provide legal protection; (5) Submit a letter to the French Consul-General and the Municipal Government requesting a stop to the demolition; (6) Elect five representatives to hold a letter requesting assistance from the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession and the Business Federations on each road. The meeting adjourned around 11 PM.
